  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b5bcf8cf-a623-4d8b-abbc-b11a8fcfcf13'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer5927017889816797543">The town psychiatrist has decided to switch everybody in Pine Cove, California, from their normal antidepressants to placebos, so naturally—well, to be accurate, artificially—business is booming at the local blues bar.   <span id="freeText5927017889816797543" style="display:none">The town psychiatrist has decided to switch everybody in Pine Cove, California, from their normal antidepressants to placebos, so naturally—well, to be accurate, artificially—business is booming at the local blues bar. Trouble is, those lonely slide-guitar notes have also attracted a colossal sea beast named Steve with, shall we say, a thing for explosive oil tanker trucks. Suddenly, morose Pine Cove turns libidinous and is hit by a mysterious crime wave, and a beleaguered constable has to fight off his own gonzo appetites to find out what's wrong and what, if anything, to do about it.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346444915" />
    <a title="Karl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1935255-karl"><img alt="Karl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588969235p2/1935255.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2346444915?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karl" href="/user/show/1935255-karl">Karl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780380975068" href="/book/show/1095789.The_Lust_Lizard_of_Melancholy_Cove">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346444915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14293319297983165496">“The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove” by Christopher Moore takes place in Pine Cove a small Pacific coast town of 5000. Over a third of the population served by local Dr. Valerie Riordan, has been rendered dependent on antidepressants.<br/><br/>Obsessive/compulsive cleaning freak, Bess Leander, is found hanged from a calico cloth rope, a possible suicide, and her friend Val fears she may have been overmedicating. Investigating the death, is the stoned town constable, Theophilus Crowe. <br/><br/>Val next blackmails f</span>
  <span id="freeText14293319297983165496" style="display:none">“The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove” by Christopher Moore takes place in Pine Cove a small Pacific coast town of 5000. Over a third of the population served by local Dr. Valerie Riordan, has been rendered dependent on antidepressants.<br /><br />Obsessive/compulsive cleaning freak, Bess Leander, is found hanged from a calico cloth rope, a possible suicide, and her friend Val fears she may have been overmedicating. Investigating the death, is the stoned town constable, Theophilus Crowe. <br /><br />Val next blackmails fish-fetishist and local pharmacist Winston Krauss into giving all antidepressant users in town placebos instead of their regular medication. As the antidepressants wear off, a hilariously uncontrollable erotic revolution takes place in the formerly groggy and uninspired population. A simultaneous nuclear plant leak into the ocean awakens a serotonin-deficit sea beast named Steve, who descends on the town, who is disguised occasionally as a double-wide mobile home. <br /><br />Enter Delta guitarist Catfish Jefferson who has recently been hired to play at the local ‘Head of the Slug Saloon’, where his marvelously sad blues has added to the local scene’s seductive narcosis. Fifty years ago down on the Delta, Catfish first met the Sea Beast, the hundred foot creature, Steve, that loved his steel guitar sound and has now risen from the depths.<br /><br />This is laugh out loud funny and a bit zany at times. <br /><br />This copy is signed by the author Christopher Moore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14293319297983165496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_535821465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/535821465" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/535821465?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer535821465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4850414197760949417">I've heard many good things about Christopher Moore, but mostly I've heard that I'd love his sense of humor. In life, I take two things seriously: The health and security of my family. Everything else is fair game. If you can riff on religion, politics, sex and the overall human condition, in a thought-provoking, sarcastic manner, you will find a friend in me. For this reason, I would love to just sit down and have a conversation with Moore. I'm sure we'd laugh ourselves stupid.<br/><br/>The Characters: A</span>
  <span id="freeText4850414197760949417" style="display:none">I've heard many good things about Christopher Moore, but mostly I've heard that I'd love his sense of humor. In life, I take two things seriously: The health and security of my family. Everything else is fair game. If you can riff on religion, politics, sex and the overall human condition, in a thought-provoking, sarcastic manner, you will find a friend in me. For this reason, I would love to just sit down and have a conversation with Moore. I'm sure we'd laugh ourselves stupid.<br /><br />The Characters: A pothead constable, an aging b-movie actress, a psychiatrist, a biologist, a blues man, a painter, a pharmacist with a sexual preference for sea life and a barkeep that's more metal and silicone than human, make up the cast of The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove. And those are just the good guys. Somehow, Moore makes each of these people flesh and blood real. I even felt bad for the fish-f***ing druggist. I love well drawn characters, no matter how outlandish, and Moore delivers by the bucket-load.<br /><br />Now, I didn't read the synopsis of this book because someone warned me that Harper (Moore's publisher) tends to ruin some of the funnier moments with their blurbs, so I went into this book blind, aside from the title of course. When Steve the Sea Beast finds his first lover around page 60, I almost lost my mind laughing. Which brings me to the synopsis. Harper actually covers that scene in the blurb, so I was very happy I skipped the spoiler. <br /><br />There's far too much going on in this book to cover even a quarter of it here, but I will say Moore is now one of my favorite authors. One of the other warnings I was given before reading this book was that The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove was his most lackluster work to date, so if I enjoyed this book, I'd love his other stuff. We'll see about that. All I know is that I've never laughed so hard while reading. Ever. Period. The last forty pages of this novel had my sides hurting. <br /><br />The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove is a far-fetched, foul-mouthed, filthy-minded pedestrian, walking the streets of the Land of Make Believe. If you like your humor lewd and crude, but interlaced with witty social commentary, you will adore Christopher Moore.<br /><br />E.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4850414197760949417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1343129356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1343129356" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598976963p2/6753400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1343129356?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=cheer-up">cheer-up</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1343129356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15249812723501000763">What would happen if all the inhabitants of a small California town were suddenly off their anti-depressants? Well, the local bar would probably see a boom in business. The general libido would also probably go up a notch. Some people's behavior might become a bit erratic. All this would make life more than a little complicated for the small town's adorable and hopelessly high police constable, Theo. And just to add to Theo's already messy life, an old bluesman decides to set up shop at the afor</span>
  <span id="freeText15249812723501000763" style="display:none">What would happen if all the inhabitants of a small California town were suddenly off their anti-depressants? Well, the local bar would probably see a boom in business. The general libido would also probably go up a notch. Some people's behavior might become a bit erratic. All this would make life more than a little complicated for the small town's adorable and hopelessly high police constable, Theo. And just to add to Theo's already messy life, an old bluesman decides to set up shop at the aforementioned local dive: his menlancholy tunes wake up an ancient beast with an axe to grind… and weird urges to fulfill.<br /><br />If the idea of a mildly insane B-movie actress and a sea monster having a deep romantic bond is something that weirds you out, my advice is to not read this book. Christopher Moore writes for people who like to stretch the suspension of disbelief to extremes, who find salty humor delightful and who think that weird stuff is just a part of life. I love him.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong: in theory, a story about a dinosaur emitting pheromones that drive everyone to frenetically fornicate within a 10-mile radius, while meth dealers do their thing, forcing the one utterly unqualified law enforcement officer to deal with organised crime and an entire town gone mad, could easy become crass and uninteresting. Except Moore writes with heart and laughter, he develops fucked up characters who are human, fun and endearing. That makes the utter ridiculousness of naming a sea monster Steve adorable and hilarious. This book is a great little adventure filled with uncontrollable giggles and oddball characters and I loved it!<br /><br />If you like zany and twisted humor and haven't read anything by Christopher Moore yet, this is a great place to start. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15249812723501000763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Hamilton, take note.<br /><br />'Steve' stirs up the animal spirits of the low-seritonin residents of Pine Cove (aka Cambria) -- of which there are many, as the town's sole psychiatrist has cut off their Prozac, surreptitiosly substituting sugar-pill placebos, with the connivance of the town's sole pharmacist, who satisfies his carnal urges with an inflatable dolphin in his bathtub....<br /><br />[Dr. Val] came out of her office to find her new receptionist, Chloe, furiously masturbating, "her steno chair squeaking like a tortured squirrel."<br /><br />"Sorry," Chloe said, a bit later... <div id="review_38130169" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38130169" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411956191p2/1219253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38130169?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes a good laugh</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38130169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4744159970791915742">Christopher Moore is, as always, a genius when it comes to the absurd and warped sense of humor that I enjoy oh-so-much. Who else could give us a plot that includes all of the following: a former B movie starlet who still lives the life of her most famous role as Kendra: Warrior Babe of the Wasteland, a sea beast with a vendetta against a wayward bluesman, a psychologist who decides to put the entire town on placebo anti-depressants instead of the real deal, a pharmacist with a fish fetish (yes,</span>
  <span id="freeText4744159970791915742" style="display:none">Christopher Moore is, as always, a genius when it comes to the absurd and warped sense of humor that I enjoy oh-so-much. Who else could give us a plot that includes all of the following: a former B movie starlet who still lives the life of her most famous role as Kendra: Warrior Babe of the Wasteland, a sea beast with a vendetta against a wayward bluesman, a psychologist who decides to put the entire town on placebo anti-depressants instead of the real deal, a pharmacist with a fish fetish (yes, that's right), meth labs and drug dealers, interspecies love, and occasional chapters told from the point of view of a labrador retriever named Skinner? This is not for everyone--serious people need not apply. The plot is wacky and unbelievable; in other words, vintage Moore. While I really enjoyed the book and laughed often, the only reason I gave it 3 stars is that, when compared with his other books, I didn't like it quite as much as Bloodsucking Fiends and Fluke (Or I Know Why the Winged Whale Sings). However, the novel is well worth the time of anyone who already enjoys Moore or is discovering him for the first time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4744159970791915742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_47079634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47079634" />
    <a title="Yael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1714801-yael"><img alt="Yael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226624084p2/1714801.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47079634?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yael" href="/user/show/1714801-yael">Yael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47079634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2496591293177906103">Valerie Riordan, the sole psychotherapist in Pine Cove, California, has switched all her patients' antidepressants to placebos -- a reaction to the apparent suicide of Bess Leander, one of her patients, who, Val thought, might have lived had Val done more talk therapy and less drug therapy. As a result, business is booming at The Head of the Slug, the local Blues bar, run by Mavis, whose clients swear that underneath her ancient, wrinkled, liver-spotted skin there lurks the Terminator. Problem: </span>
  <span id="freeText2496591293177906103" style="display:none">Valerie Riordan, the sole psychotherapist in Pine Cove, California, has switched all her patients' antidepressants to placebos -- a reaction to the apparent suicide of Bess Leander, one of her patients, who, Val thought, might have lived had Val done more talk therapy and less drug therapy. As a result, business is booming at The Head of the Slug, the local Blues bar, run by Mavis, whose clients swear that underneath her ancient, wrinkled, liver-spotted skin there lurks the Terminator. Problem: those lonely Blues notes from her new hire, Catfish Jefferson, have attracted the attention of an enormous, 5,000-year-old marine reptile named Steve who has a <i>thing</i> for petroleum tanker trucks.<br /><br />With the advent of Steve, Pine Cove suddenly turns lustful and is hit by a weird crime wave with no understandable explanation. So Theophilus Crowe, the town constable, must find out what's wrong and what to do about it.<br /><br />Enter all our other old friends from other novels of Moore's -- Molly Michon, the aging but still-beautiful and deadly Warrior Babe of the Outland (well, she <i>was</i>, until a stupid accident that wasn't her fault left her with a scar that got her canned by the movie studio); Mavis, proprietor of The Head of the Slug (originally named "The Head of the Wolf," but the local Greens decided the name was cruel to animals and forced her to change it); Dr. Val, the aforementioned psychiatrist; H. P., proprietor of H. P.'s Cafe, which features delicious delicacies such as Eggs Sothoth; Skinner, the happy-go-lucky idiot dog belonging to the Food Guy, biologist Gabe Fenton; and numerous others. Enter also some local villians who do meet timely, deserved, and hilarious ends, such as Sheriff John Burton, whose ranch hides a nasty secret, and who has been blackmailing pothead Theophilus Crowe into being the town constable for years; and Joseph Leander, the late Bess Leander's adulterous, murderous husband. With a less-than-together supporting cast of -- well, check them out for yourself.<br /><br />As one reviewer said, Christopher Moore must have been laughing his head off while writing <i>The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove</i>, and likely taking hits of nitrous oxide between sentences. The title alone is worth the price of the book, which could be substituted most successfully for every antidepressant in the pharmacy.<br /><br />As a bonus, the biomedical and scientific aspects of this novel were researched down to the bare bones by the author. All that is missing from it is a lawsuit by Toho Productions for inappropriate appropriation of their star character (we know who he is!) -- and that may be forthcoming at any time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2496591293177906103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18266271874786225868"><i>The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove</i> is a warm-hearted probe into the meaning of inter-species fornication; Fornication with giant lizards, sea mammals, gas trucks, and a ex-soft porn movie actress in Xena costumes with broad swords. In other words, just another day in Christopher Moore's brain. The author has his brain working over-time in this silly little romp. Maybe a little too silly even for Moore. Yet it remains very funny and entertaining. Moore revives some of his Pine Cove residents incl</span>
  <span id="freeText18266271874786225868" style="display:none"><i>The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove</i> is a warm-hearted probe into the meaning of inter-species fornication; Fornication with giant lizards, sea mammals, gas trucks, and a ex-soft porn movie actress in Xena costumes with broad swords. In other words, just another day in Christopher Moore's brain. The author has his brain working over-time in this silly little romp. Maybe a little too silly even for Moore. Yet it remains very funny and entertaining. Moore revives some of his Pine Cove residents including H. P., Mavis, and the grass smoking sheriff, Theopolis Crow. Add Molly Michon, a has-been starlet and Steve, a perpetually horny sea lizard and you get the idea this is not exactly <i>Cannery Row</i>. But if you can't handle kinky situations and over-the-top slapstick comedy, why are you even considering a Christopher Moore novel?</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153650824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8151100047329982502">I just finished reading this, and as I explained to my fiancee last night when I couldn't stop reading it: it does not hold up the qualities that are necessary for me to classify a book a good book; however it is great escapism. The characters are not real. The author does nor reveal anything to me in the telling of the story. He has awareness that he is writing escapism and I like that. He is not your typical escapism writer like James Patterson or John Grisham who turn out one load of crap aft</span>
  <span id="freeText8151100047329982502" style="display:none">I just finished reading this, and as I explained to my fiancee last night when I couldn't stop reading it: it does not hold up the qualities that are necessary for me to classify a book a good book; however it is great escapism. The characters are not real. The author does nor reveal anything to me in the telling of the story. He has awareness that he is writing escapism and I like that. He is not your typical escapism writer like James Patterson or John Grisham who turn out one load of crap after another, but never stop taking themselves seriously. <br /><br />I like that his books are fun to read and I typically laugh out loud a few times during the read. Compared to my normal depressing books, it is nice to laugh and not think too much about everything he is trying to say. <br /><br />If you have read any of Moore's books you know exactly what I am talking about. This one was better than the last two in the vampire series he was doing, but not as good as some of his more well known books. <br /><br />I recommend it, if you are in a rut and just want to laugh a little, this book is great for that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8151100047329982502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47486071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17291779639895501873">Where to start? Where to start?<br/><br/>This book was my maiden dip into Christopher Moore, who should get a Pulitzer for his titles alone! Who can pass up a title like this? I have since moved on to read several other of his books. <br/><br/>Totally improbable, quirky, witty and twisted. My kind of humor. <br/><br/>From the tale of the Bluesman Catfish Jefferson, to poor Steve the Sea Monster, looking for love in all the wrong fuel trucks, to Molly and her narrator, the story just flowed. I loved the way Moorse chose to de</span>
  <span id="freeText17291779639895501873" style="display:none">Where to start? Where to start?<br /><br />This book was my maiden dip into Christopher Moore, who should get a Pulitzer for his titles alone! Who can pass up a title like this? I have since moved on to read several other of his books. <br /><br />Totally improbable, quirky, witty and twisted. My kind of humor. <br /><br />From the tale of the Bluesman Catfish Jefferson, to poor Steve the Sea Monster, looking for love in all the wrong fuel trucks, to Molly and her narrator, the story just flowed. I loved the way Moorse chose to describe things-<br />ie <i>"It wasn't that their (the townpeople) anxiety was gone, but rather that it ran off their backs like warm rain off a naked toddler who had just discovered the splash and magic of mud".</i><br /><br />Or Moore's creative if somewhat unorthodox use of a weed wacker. Or of Skinner the dog's perspective of life "Danger, Food Guy! Danger." <br /><br />Anyhow, I guess you can gather that I liked it...liked it enough to send it on to some very special folks Down Under, in the hopes that it can get released at the Aussie 2005 Convention.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17291779639895501873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15120960158824604948"><b>2.5</b><br/><br/>You have to be high to read this. <br/>Or drunk. <br/>Or both. Yes, both would be best. Otherwise, the sheer amount of exaggerations would make you crazy. <br/><br/>With its title alone, you have to assume you'd have to suspend your disbelief completely. I don't mind that at all.   <span id="freeText15120960158824604948" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b><br /><br />You have to be high to read this. <br />Or drunk. <br />Or both. Yes, both would be best. Otherwise, the sheer amount of exaggerations would make you crazy. <br /><br />With its title alone, you have to assume you'd have to suspend your disbelief completely. I don't mind that at all. It is supposed to be a silly book after all. But you don't get <i>any</i> respite from all the exaggerations. It's just goes on an on, one crazy situation or a person after another. After a while one gets tired of it.<br /><br />I wonder if I am too serious to appreciate the type of humour in this book. <br /></span>

<div id="review_981503783" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/981503783" />
    <a title="John S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32668942-john-s"><img alt="John S" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/981503783?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John S" href="/user/show/32668942-john-s">John S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6436566-the-lust-lizard-of-melancholy-cove">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer981503783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15472308253179043697">Brief Synopsis: 'Lust Lizard' is set in Pine Cove, a small coastal town in Cali where the majority of the town has been taken off their anti-depressants on a whim by the one psychiatrist in town. There is a enormous sea creature masquerading as a trailer who happens to make people very horny (yes you read that sentence right). While all of this is happening, there is a underbelly of crime just simmering and waiting to overflow. Sound fun? Well it is.<br/><br/>Unlike Moore's other books, this one does take</span>
  <span id="freeText15472308253179043697" style="display:none">Brief Synopsis: 'Lust Lizard' is set in Pine Cove, a small coastal town in Cali where the majority of the town has been taken off their anti-depressants on a whim by the one psychiatrist in town. There is a enormous sea creature masquerading as a trailer who happens to make people very horny (yes you read that sentence right). While all of this is happening, there is a underbelly of crime just simmering and waiting to overflow. Sound fun? Well it is.<br /><br />Unlike Moore's other books, this one does take a while to get going. The absurd and hilarious doesn't present itself much before 70 to 80 pages in, but to his credit, he is developing characters during that time. Each chapter is written with intention to focus on the thought process of one character. Every character has his or her own sense of charm and quirky habits. You have a stoner constable who is best friends with a recluse biologist who owns a dog named Skinner (funniest internal monologue btw). Those are just three of many. Each character gets ample time to develop, and each forms their own tapestry very well.<br /><br />There is nothing amazing or outstanding about the plot. The elements are all incredibly odd and don't seem like they would mesh quite right. (How can you expect a leather clad, broad sword wielding warrior princess to mix with a 80 year old blues singer???) But somehow it works. Yet, it all boils down to a simple, easy read. It's all in the presentation that makes this a hilarious ride.<br /><br />This books goes places you would never expect with characters that you would never imagine. Its a great read, one you should take.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15472308253179043697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204802295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17493824736985048164">I'm not sure how this book ended up in my bookshelves, but there it was. As you may be able to guess from the title, this is not serious literature. The story takes place in a small town on the coast, where a 5,000 year old sea monster has been awakened. He has a taste for warm blooded animals, so he proceeds into town to snack on the townfolk. The unlikely hero of the story is the pothead town constable Theo Crowe. Theo and his friends decide to help the sea monster return to the sea, so he doe</span>
  <span id="freeText17493824736985048164" style="display:none">I'm not sure how this book ended up in my bookshelves, but there it was. As you may be able to guess from the title, this is not serious literature. The story takes place in a small town on the coast, where a 5,000 year old sea monster has been awakened. He has a taste for warm blooded animals, so he proceeds into town to snack on the townfolk. The unlikely hero of the story is the pothead town constable Theo Crowe. Theo and his friends decide to help the sea monster return to the sea, so he doesn't get hunted down and killed. Fortunately for everyone involved, the sea monster has only eaten badguys, so it's easy to root for him. Complete nonsense, this is a quick read, which leaves the reader as soon as the last page has been turned. Mindless escapism.</span>

          </span>

I usually enjoy the first half of his books more than the second half; I suppose it’s because I like his characters more than his ridiculous plots.<br /> <br />This story returns to Pine Cove, where the inhabitants are going a little nuts, because in a fit of misplaced guilt, the local psychiatrist has taken all of her patients off their antidepressant medications. Also a giant sea monster has come ashore and is psychically transmitting lust to the locals.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2172893159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2172893159" />
    <a title="David Benefry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15600591-david-benefry"><img alt="David Benefry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502115613p2/15600591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2172893159?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Benefry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Benefry" href="/user/show/15600591-david-benefry">David Benefry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2172893159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14332782921674751609">“The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove” by Christopher Moore – A Revolution of Lizards and Placebos<br/><br/>Christopher Moore's Pine Cove<br/><br/>A few strange things have been happening in the quaint town of Pine Cove. To begin with, the doctor has about a third of the population on antidepressants, but after an obsessive-compulsive patient commits suicide, the good doc Valerie Riordan finds herself at fault. After blackmailing the fish fetishist and pharmacist, she ensures that all of her patients are now receivin</span>
  <span id="freeText14332782921674751609" style="display:none">“The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove” by Christopher Moore – A Revolution of Lizards and Placebos<br /><br />Christopher Moore's Pine Cove<br /><br />A few strange things have been happening in the quaint town of Pine Cove. To begin with, the doctor has about a third of the population on antidepressants, but after an obsessive-compulsive patient commits suicide, the good doc Valerie Riordan finds herself at fault. After blackmailing the fish fetishist and pharmacist, she ensures that all of her patients are now receiving placebos instead of the real medication they need. At the same time, a radiation leak from a nuclear power plant is seeping deep into the water and awakening something fierce, a 20-foot sea lizard named Steve... and these are the tamest of events taking place in The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove by Christopher Moore.<br /><br />If you haven't read the first book and would like to start with this one, feel free to do so at your discretion. While Moore does reuse characters from his previous books as well as reference a few things, on the whole you don't need to have read the earlier novels to understand this one. You'll probably be able to laugh at a few more passages and feel closer to some of the people, but that's about it.<br /><br />A Trove of Black Humour and Absurdity <br /><br />Virtually all of the characters in this book go through trials and tribulations of their own, and while realistically-speaking some of them wouldn't make for a laughing matter, Moore manages to twist it into the realms of comedy. <br /><br />Speaking of the people, I'd say that this book has hands-down one of the most diverse casts you'll ever find in a book. Every single character is unique and differentiated from the others in very obvious ways, all of them having major quirks and strong defining personality traits, giving them all an eccentric quality, especially Steve the giant lizard from the sea. <br /><br />The Meaning of Decadence<br /><br />While I am certain that many of his thoughts on real-life topics made it in here, such as the monopoly of the pharmaceutical industry on our daily lives, I am quite convinced that he never intended for this to be a serious adventure. The story is filled with ridiculous decadence and even some topics which a few readers might find distasteful, with there being a decent amount of immoral eroticism to be found. <br /><br />As the reader, I believe it is best to adopt the perspective that this is simply an adventure about having fun and letting go. One shouldn't over-analyze anything or try to grasp for some kind of greater meaning.<br /><br />The Final Verdict<br /><br />It seems that Christopher has done it yet again, penning a novel far outside the limits imposed by rules and conventions. It's a savage and unrelenting story that takes us to the very outer edges of surrealism and ridicule, exploring lands very few authors would ever dare venturing into. It's a deeply-humorous book that offers a drastically different experience from virtually all the other novels out there, and if that's the kind of insanity which attracts you, then I have to wholeheartedly recommend this book for you.<br /><br />This was an abridged version of our review. If you'd like to read the full one, you can do so here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bookwormex.com/lust-lizard-melancholy-cove-christopher-moore-review/">https://bookwormex.com/lust-lizard-me...</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14332782921674751609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_376344905" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/376344905" />
    <a title="Donna LaValley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4162429-donna-lavalley"><img alt="Donna LaValley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1282004714p2/4162429.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/376344905?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna LaValley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna LaValley" href="/user/show/4162429-donna-lavalley">Donna LaValley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer376344905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10449637026369775824">The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove followed Christopher Moore’s successful debut novel, Practical Demonkeeping. I don’t know if he was high on his new popularity or high on something else, but this one disappoints, with colorful new characters being the only saving graces.<br/><br/>Still in Pine Cove, California, some of the same characters (and the new ones) again must confront something supernatural, although the giant Sea Beast “lizard” comes from deep in the ocean and has only one non-known animal cha</span>
  <span id="freeText10449637026369775824" style="display:none">The Lust Lizard of Melancholy Cove followed Christopher Moore’s successful debut novel, Practical Demonkeeping. I don’t know if he was high on his new popularity or high on something else, but this one disappoints, with colorful new characters being the only saving graces.<br /><br />Still in Pine Cove, California, some of the same characters (and the new ones) again must confront something supernatural, although the giant Sea Beast “lizard” comes from deep in the ocean and has only one non-known animal characteristic: s/he makes all other animal life horny and eager for sex, but more especially if those people are lonely or sad. The color and shape changes of the animal echo those of cephalopods, so that’s a “scientific” supposition. And, of course, this one devours people – but again, all of them are irritating and expendable people.<br /><br />Theophilus Crowe is the mature male whose point of view is the central one. There is always one such male, almost interchangeably so in each book, with similarly structured names – see Augustus Brine in Practical Demonkeeping. He grows marijuana, enjoys it, sometimes goes without it. He gets the Babe in the end. I enjoyed the new characters Gabe and Catfish, and the return of “Nailgun” or Spider, the internet go-to guy of the local law. The women are mostly vile (especially Mavis).<br /><br />Sometimes sex between a woman and a beast is just too crude for me, even when -or especially when- it is written for laughs. Another problem I have with this book was inconsistency. For example, 2 guys on a meth lab are eaten by the Sea Beast, and we are told such guard-and-cooker teams are constantly rotating, 24 hours a day. However, when these 2 disappear, the author forgets that the next team would notice.<br /><br />When I’m reading a book full of sex, odd characters, a crazy plot, revenge, slime, murder, and mayhem, but my mind wanders to “Gee, maybe I ought to pay some bills,” then I know that despite the occasional laugh-out-loud lines, this was a 1-star book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10449637026369775824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1192607237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192607237" />
    <a title="Glenn Conley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34812753-glenn-conley"><img alt="Glenn Conley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412894833p2/34812753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192607237?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glenn Conley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glenn Conley" href="/user/show/34812753-glenn-conley">Glenn Conley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34812753-glenn-conley?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192607237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15216096273046992746">This book is very strange. It starts out innocent enough, but just spirals out of control. It's like the author wrote the first half of the book sober, and the second half, stoned out of his fucking mind. Because the second half is just plain bat-shit crazy.<br/><br/>The story starts out nice and simple. A new sheriff comes to town. Greetings all around. Everything is fine. Nothing to see here. But then, naked people keep showing up everywhere. Fucking in the park. Fucking on the sidewalk. Fucking on the </span>
  <span id="freeText15216096273046992746" style="display:none">This book is very strange. It starts out innocent enough, but just spirals out of control. It's like the author wrote the first half of the book sober, and the second half, stoned out of his fucking mind. Because the second half is just plain bat-shit crazy.<br /><br />The story starts out nice and simple. A new sheriff comes to town. Greetings all around. Everything is fine. Nothing to see here. But then, naked people keep showing up everywhere. Fucking in the park. Fucking on the sidewalk. Fucking on the counter of the local diner, while the new sheriff is trying to drink his fucking coffee.<br /><br />It's very distracting, all these people fucking everywhere. You just can't get any goddamn work done. The fucking has got to stop, I tell yaz! So, the new sheriff gets the local shrink to prescribe some pills, to calm down the fucking hilarity. That'll work, right? Not so much.<br /><br />And then there's this huge lizard. A literal lust lizard the size of a goddamn T-Rex, that just shows up out of nowhere. It feeds on people's lust. Well, that is to say, it is the one causing all the people to fuck all the time. It sends out some signal, or pheromone, that makes people all horny and shit. And, somehow those signals draw the people to the lust lizard. To commune naked, and offer themselves up to the lizard as sacrifices, or some bullshit.<br /><br />See? Mr. Moore was smoking some good crack when he wrote the last bit of this book. It's fucking crazy. It doesn't make any goddamn sense. But I guess, at least it was a tad bit amusing. Because of all the crazy naked fucking people. And the fact that they named the big lust lizard 'Steve'. Because apparently, it looked like a Steve.<br /><br />It really cracked me up when they tried to reason with the lust lizard. "Come on, Steve... Don't eat that guy. That guy's cool. Eat that other guy, over there. He's a fucking asshole." Comedy gold, I tell ya.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15216096273046992746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qO6tbGwJ7YvmLO+rIR2XmfFokqk3LD9MWt2LLACIs0AtxvXj0wMrOYGmW/yl/imZOhxVaoW95BsvwRCXR2BUfw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sly//1cShn+Q3QEmcIMk4/WhHOFxIdGuPAr+NKjQZ2c3dOdw6BhAzfdXtXH0YJrjPtXbIsOwCvlJFmWP7ziAWA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4643698191998139054"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. </i><br/><br/>Christopher Moore is an American writer of absurdist fiction. He grew up in Mansfield, OH, and attended Ohio State University and Brooks Institute of Photography in Santa Barbara, CA.<br/><br/>Moore's novels typically involve conflicted everyman characters suddenly struggling through supernatural or extraordinary circums</span>
  <span id="freeText4643698191998139054" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. </i><br /><br />Christopher Moore is an American writer of absurdist fiction. He grew up in Mansfield, OH, and attended Ohio State University and Brooks Institute of Photography in Santa Barbara, CA.<br /><br />Moore's novels typically involve conflicted everyman characters suddenly struggling through supernatural or extraordinary circumstances. Inheriting a humanism from his love of John Steinbeck and a sense of the absurd from Kurt Vonnegut, Moore is a best-selling author with major cult status.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4643698191998139054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
